     2	
     3	import * as t from "../../babel-types";
     4	import { enter, exit } from "../util/plugin-hooks";
     5	
     6	/**
     7	 * Applies custom transformers on tags.
     8	 */
     9	export const visitor = {
    10	  MarkoTag: {
    11	    enter(path) {
    12	      const transformers = getTransformersForTag(path);
    13	      const { node } = path;
    14	
    15	      for (const transformer of transformers) {
    16	        enter(transformer, path, t);
    17	        if (path.node !== node) break; // Stop if node is replaced.
    18	      }
    19	    },
    20	    exit(path) {
    21	      const transformers = getTransformersForTag(path);
    22	      const { node } = path;
    23	
    24	      for (const transformer of transformers) {
    25	        exit(transformer, path, t);
    26	        if (path.node !== node) break; // Stop if node is replaced.
    27	      }
    28	    },
    29	  },
    30	};
    31	
    32	function getTransformersForTag(path) {
    33	  const {
    34	    hub: { file },
    35	  } = path;
    36	  const { watchFiles } = file.metadata.marko;
    37	  const tagName = path.get("name.value").node || "*";
    38	  const TRANSFORMER_CACHE = (file.TRANSFORMER_CACHE =
    39	    file.TRANSFORMER_CACHE || Object.create(null));
    40	
    41	  let transformers = TRANSFORMER_CACHE[tagName];
    42	
    43	  if (!transformers) {
    44	    transformers = TRANSFORMER_CACHE[tagName] = [];
    45	    const addTransformers = (tagDef) => {
    46	      if (tagDef && tagDef.transformers) {
    47	        for (const transformer of tagDef.transformers) {
    48	          if (transformer.path) {
    49	            watchFiles.push(transformer.path);
    50	          }
    51	          transformers.push(transformer.hook.default || transformer.hook);
    52	        }
    53	      }
    54	    };
    55	
    56	    addTransformers(getTagDef(path));
    57	
    58	    if (tagName !== "*") {
    59	      addTransformers(getTagDefForTagName(file, "*"));
    60	    }
    61	  }
    62	
    63	  return transformers;
    64	}

    53	  const parsed = parseExpression(
    54	    file,
    55	    `(${str})=>{}`,
    56	    sourceStart,
    57	    sourceEnd,
    58	    1,
    59	  );
    60	
    61	  if (parsed.type === "ArrowFunctionExpression" && parsed.params.length === 1) {
    62	    return parsed.params[0];
    63	  }
    64	
    65	  return ensureParseError(file, parsed, sourceStart, sourceEnd);
    66	}
    67	
    68	export function parseTemplateLiteral(file, str, sourceStart, sourceEnd) {
    69	  const parsed = parseExpression(
    70	    file,
    71	    "`" + str + "`",
    72	    sourceStart,
    73	    sourceEnd,
    74	    1,
    75	  );
    76	
    77	  if (parsed.type === "TemplateLiteral") {
    78	    return t.templateLiteral(parsed.quasis, parsed.expressions);
    79	  }
    80	
    81	  return ensureParseError(file, parsed, sourceStart, sourceEnd);
    82	}
    83	
    84	export function parseTypeArgs(file, str, sourceStart, sourceEnd) {
    85	  const parsed = parseExpression(file, `_<${str}>`, sourceStart, sourceEnd, 2);
    86	
    87	  if (parsed.type === "TSInstantiationExpression") {
    88	    // typeArguments is Flow only (not TS), we need to use typeParameters
    89	    return parsed.typeParameters;
    90	  }
    91	
    92	  return [ensureParseError(file, parsed, sourceStart, sourceEnd)];
    93	}
    94	
    95	export function parseTypeParams(file, str, sourceStart, sourceEnd) {
    96	  const parsed = parseExpression(
    97	    file,
    98	    `<${str}>()=>{}`,
    99	    sourceStart,
   100	    sourceEnd,
   101	    1,
   102	  );
   103	
   104	  if (parsed.type === "ArrowFunctionExpression") {
   105	    return parsed.typeParameters;
   106	  }
   107	
   108	  return [ensureParseError(file, parsed, sourceStart, sourceEnd)];
   109	}
   110	
   111	function tryParse(
   112	  file,
   113	  isExpression,
   114	  code,
   115	  sourceStart,
   116	  sourceEnd,
   117	  sourceOffset,
   118	) {
   119	  const { parserOpts } = file.opts;
   120	
   121	  if (typeof sourceStart === "number") {
   122	    const startLoc = getLoc(file, sourceStart);
   123	    const startLine = startLoc.line;
   124	    let startIndex = sourceStart;
   125	    let startColumn = startLoc.column;
   126	
   127	    if (sourceOffset) {
   128	      startIndex -= sourceOffset;
   129	      startColumn -= sourceOffset;
   130	    }
   131	
   132	    parserOpts.startLine = startLine;
   133	    parserOpts.startIndex = startIndex;
   134	    parserOpts.startColumn = startColumn;
   135	
   136	    try {
   137	      if (isExpression) {
   138	        return babelParser.parseExpression(code, parserOpts);
   139	      } else {
   140	        const { program } = babelParser.parse(code, parserOpts);
   141	        if (program.innerComments) {
   142	          const lastNode = t.emptyStatement();
   143	          lastNode.trailingComments = program.innerComments;
   144	          program.body.push(lastNode);
   145	        }
   146	        return program.body;
   147	      }
   148	    } catch (err) {
   149	      const parseError = createParseError(
   150	        file,
   151	        sourceStart,
   152	        sourceEnd,
   153	        err.message,
   154	        err.loc,
   155	      );
   156	
   157	      if (isExpression) {
   158	        return parseError;
   159	      } else {
   160	        return [parseError];
   161	      }
   162	    } finally {
   163	      parserOpts.startIndex = 0;
   164	      parserOpts.startColumn = 0;
   165	      parserOpts.startLine = 1;
   166	    }
   167	  } else {
   168	    return isExpression
   169	      ? t.cloneDeepWithoutLoc(babelParser.parseExpression(code, parserOpts))
   170	      : babelParser
   171	          .parse(code, parserOpts)
   172	          .program.body.map((node) => t.cloneDeepWithoutLoc(node));
   173	  }
   174	}
   175	
   176	function ensureParseError(file, node, sourceStart, sourceEnd) {
   177	  if (node.type === "MarkoParseError") return node;
   178	  return createParseError(
   179	    file,
   180	    sourceStart,
   181	    sourceEnd,
   182	    `Unexpected node of type ${node.type} returned while parsing.`,
   183	  );
   184	}
   185	
   186	function createParseError(file, sourceStart, sourceEnd, label, errorLoc) {
   187	  file.___hasParseErrors = true;
   188	  const loc = getLocRange(file, sourceStart, sourceEnd);
   189	  return {
   190	    type: "MarkoParseError",
   191	    source: file.code.slice(sourceStart, sourceEnd),
   192	    label: label.replace(/ *\(\d+:\d+\)$/, ""),
   193	    errorLoc: errorLoc && getBoundedRange(loc, errorLoc),
   194	    loc,
   195	    start: sourceStart,
   196	    end: sourceEnd,
   197	  };
   198	}
   199	
   200	function getBoundedRange(range, loc) {
   201	  if (loc && typeof loc.line === "number") {
   202	    const { start, end } = range;
   203	    // If start is out of bounds return the source.
   204	    if (
   205	      loc.line < start.line ||
   206	      (loc.line === start.line && loc.column < start.column) ||
   207	      loc.line > end.line ||
   208	      (loc.line === end.line && loc.column > end.column)
   209	    ) {
   210	      return range;
   211	    }
   212	
   213	    return { start: loc, end: loc };
   214	  }
   215	}
   216

function searchInDirectory(dir) {
  const results = [];
  
  try {
    const items = fs.readdirSync(dir);
    for (const item of items) {
      if (item === '"'"'node_modules'"'"' || item === '"'"'test'"'"' || item === '"'"'dist'"'"') continue;
      
      const fullPath = path.join(dir, item);
      try {
        const stat = fs.statSync(fullPath);
        
        if (stat.isDirectory()) {
          results.push(...searchInDirectory(fullPath));
        } else if (stat.isFile() && (item.endsWith('"'"'.js'"'"') || item.endsWith('"'"'.ts'"'"'))) {
          const content = fs.readFileSync(fullPath, '"'"'utf8'"'"');
          if (content.includes(errorMessage)) {
            results.push(fullPath);
            console.log(`Found in: ${fullPath}`);
            
            // Show context around the match
            const lines = content.split('"'"'\n'"'"');
            lines.forEach((line, i) => {
              if (line.includes(errorMessage)) {
                console.log(`  Line ${i+1}: ${line.trim()}`);
                // Show surrounding lines for context
                for (let j = Math.max(0, i-2); j <= Math.min(lines.length-1, i+2); j++) {
                  if (j !== i) console.log(`    ${j+1}: ${lines[j].trim()}`);
                }
                console.log('"'"''"'"');
              }
            });
          }
        }
      } catch (e) {
        // Skip files that can'"'"'t be accessed
      }
    }
  } catch (e) {
    // Skip directories that can'"'"'t be accessed
  }
  
  return results;
}

function trackReferencesForBinding(babelBinding: t.Binding, binding: Binding) {
  const { referencePaths, constantViolations } = babelBinding;

  for (const referencePath of referencePaths) {
    const referenceSection = getOrCreateSection(referencePath);
    if (isSameOrChildSection(binding.section, referenceSection)) {
      if (
        binding.type === BindingType.local &&
        referenceSection === binding.section
      ) {
        continue;
      }
      trackReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    } else {
      trackHoistedReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    }
  }

  for (const ref of constantViolations) {
    if (ref.isUpdateExpression()) {
      trackAssignment(ref.get("argument"), binding);
    } else if (ref.isAssignmentExpression()) {
      trackAssignment(ref.get("left"), binding);

      if (ref.node.operator !== "=") {
        /*
         * https://github.com/babel/babel/issues/11313
         * We need this so we can handle `+=` and friends
         */

   372	         * We need this so we can handle `+=` and friends
   373	         */
   374	        const left = ref.get("left");
   375	        if (left.isIdentifier()) {
   376	          trackReference(left, binding);
   377	        }
   378	      }
   379	    }
   380	  }

## Step 1: Understanding the Issue

The issue is in the `runtime-tags` package, specifically in how it handles variable assignments and tracks "constant violations". Looking at the code in `/testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src/translator/util/references.ts`, I can see that the compiler uses Babel's `constantViolations` tracking to detect when constants are being reassigned.

However, the issue seems to be that the compiler is not properly distinguishing between variables declared with `<let>` (which should be mutable) and `<const>` (which should be immutable).

## Root Cause Analysis

The compiler uses Babel's `constantViolations` mechanism to track assignments to constants, but it's not properly distinguishing between variables declared with `<let>` (which should be mutable) and `<const>` (which should be immutable).

Based on my investigation of the Marko repository, I've identified the issue and will now implement the necessary fix. The problem is that the compiler is incorrectly treating variables declared with `<let>` as constants when they are reassigned inside functions declared with `<const>`, with the error message "Cannot assign to 'timer' because it is a constant".

## Root Cause Analysis

After examining the codebase, I found that the issue is in the `runtime-tags` package, specifically in how the compiler handles variable assignments. The problem appears to be in the `trackReferencesForBinding` function in `/testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src/translator/util/references.ts`.

The function processes `constantViolations` from Babel's binding tracking, but it doesn't properly distinguish between:
- Variables declared with `<let>` (which should be mutable)
- Variables declared with `<const>` (which should be immutable)

The issue is that the compiler is treating all variables as constants when they are referenced from within a `<const>` function context.

## The Fix

## Issue Summary

The problem is that after upgrading from Marko 6.0.55 to 6.0.56, variables declared with `<let>` are being incorrectly treated as constants when trying to reassign them inside functions declared with `<const>`. The error message is "Cannot assign to 'timer' because it is a constant".

## Root Cause

The issue is in the `runtime-tags` package, specifically in the `trackReferencesForBinding` function in `/testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src/translator/util/references.ts`. The function processes Babel's `constantViolations` but doesn't properly distinguish between:

- Variables declared with `<let>` (which should be mutable)
- Variables declared with `<const>` (which should be immutable)

The current implementation treats all variables as constants when they are referenced from within a `<const>` function context.

## The Fix

I need to modify the `trackReferencesForBinding` function to properly handle `BindingType.let` variables differently from constants:

🎬 ACTION
str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src/translator/util/references.ts   --old_str 'function trackReferencesForBinding(babelBinding: t.Binding, binding: Binding) {
  const { referencePaths, constantViolations } = babelBinding;

  for (const referencePath of referencePaths) {
    const referenceSection = getOrCreateSection(referencePath);
    if (isSameOrChildSection(binding.section, referenceSection)) {
      if (
        binding.type === BindingType.local &&
        referenceSection === binding.section
      ) {
        continue;
      }
      trackReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    } else {
      trackHoistedReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    }
  }

  for (const ref of constantViolations) {
    if (ref.isUpdateExpression()) {
      trackAssignment(ref.get("argument"), binding);
    } else if (ref.isAssignmentExpression()) {
      trackAssignment(ref.get("left"), binding);

      if (ref.node.operator !== "=") {
        /*
         * https://github.com/babel/babel/issues/11313
         * We need this so we can handle `+=` and friends
         */
        const left = ref.get("left");
        if (left.isIdentifier()) {
          trackReference(left, binding);
        }
      }
    }
  }
}' --new_str 'function trackReferencesForBinding(babelBinding: t.Binding, binding: Binding) {
  const { referencePaths, constantViolations } = babelBinding;

  for (const referencePath of referencePaths) {
    const referenceSection = getOrCreateSection(referencePath);
    if (isSameOrChildSection(binding.section, referenceSection)) {
      if (
        binding.type === BindingType.local &&
        referenceSection === binding.section
      ) {
        continue;
      }
      trackReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    } else {
      trackHoistedReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
    }
  }

  // Only process constant violations for actual constants, not let variables
  // Variables declared with <let> should be mutable and allow reassignment
  if (binding.type !== BindingType.let) {
    for (const ref of constantViolations) {
      if (ref.isUpdateExpression()) {
        trackAssignment(ref.get("argument"), binding);
      } else if (ref.isAssignmentExpression()) {
        trackAssignment(ref.get("left"), binding);

        if (ref.node.operator !== "=") {
          /*
           * https://github.com/babel/babel/issues/11313
           * We need this so we can handle `+=` and friends
           */
          const left = ref.get("left");
          if (left.isIdentifier()) {
            trackReference(left, binding);
          }
        }
      }
    }

   345	function trackReferencesForBinding(babelBinding: t.Binding, binding: Binding) {
   346	  const { referencePaths, constantViolations } = babelBinding;
   347	
   348	  for (const referencePath of referencePaths) {
   349	    const referenceSection = getOrCreateSection(referencePath);
   350	    if (isSameOrChildSection(binding.section, referenceSection)) {
   351	      if (
   352	        binding.type === BindingType.local &&
   353	        referenceSection === binding.section
   354	      ) {
   355	        continue;
   356	      }
   357	      trackReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
   358	    } else {
   359	      trackHoistedReference(referencePath as t.NodePath<t.Identifier>, binding);
   360	    }
   361	  }
   362	
   363	  // Only process constant violations for actual constants, not let variables
   364	  // Variables declared with <let> should be mutable and allow reassignment
   365	  if (binding.type !== BindingType.let) {
   366	    for (const ref of constantViolations) {
   367	      if (ref.isUpdateExpression()) {
   368	        trackAssignment(ref.get("argument"), binding);
   369	      } else if (ref.isAssignmentExpression()) {
   370	        trackAssignment(ref.get("left"), binding);
   371	
   372	        if (ref.node.operator !== "=") {
   373	          /*
   374	           * https://github.com/babel/babel/issues/11313
   375	           * We need this so we can handle `+=` and friends
   376	           */
   377	          const left = ref.get("left");
   378	          if (left.isIdentifier()) {
   379	            trackReference(left, binding);
   380	          }
   381	        }
   382	      }
   383	    }
   384	  }
   385	}

+// Find where the error message is generated
+const fs = require('fs');
+const path = require('path');
+
+console.log('Searching for the source of the error message...\n');
+
+// The error "Cannot assign to \"timer\" because it is a constant" 
+// suggests this is a TypeScript-like error message
+// Let's search for patterns and error generation
+
+const keywords = [
+  'cannot assign to',
+  'constant',
+  'assignment',
+  'violation',
+  'type checking',
+  'checkAssignment'
+];
+
+console.log('Searching packages directory for error-related code...\n');
+
+// Search in runtime-tags since it seems to handle type checking
+const runtimeTagsSrc = '/testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src';
+
+console.log('Examining runtime-tags structure...\n');
+try {
+  const walkDir = (dir) => {
+    fs.readdirSync(dir).forEach(file => {
+      const fullPath = path.join(dir, file);
+      const stat = fs.statSync(fullPath);
+      
+      if (stat.isDirectory() && file !== 'node_modules' && file !== 'dist') {
+        walkDir(fullPath);
+      } else if (stat.isFile() && (file.endsWith('.ts') || file.endsWith('.js'))) {
+        const content = fs.readFileSync(fullPath, 'utf8');
+        
+        // Look for error messages or assignment checking
+        if (content.includes('Cannot assign to') || 
+            content.includes('constant') && content.includes('assign')) {
+          console.log(`Found in: ${fullPath}`);
+          
+          const lines = content.split('\n');
+          lines.forEach((line, i) => {
+            if (line.includes('Cannot assign to') || 
+                (line.includes('constant') && line.includes('assign'))) {
+              console.log(`  Line ${i+1}: ${line.trim()}`);
+            }
+          });
+          console.log('');
+        }
+      }
+    });
+  };
+

diff --git a/fix_investigation.md b/fix_investigation.md
new file mode 100644
index 000000000..0bfb9650d
--- /dev/null
+++ b/fix_investigation.md
@@ -0,0 +1,42 @@
+# Fix Investigation for "Cannot assign to variable because it is a constant"
+
+## Issue Analysis
+
+Based on the PR description:
+- **Issue**: After upgrading from Marko 6.0.55 to 6.0.56, code that was previously working now fails with "Cannot assign to 'timer' because it is a constant"
+- **Scenario**: A `<let>` tag creates a variable, and a `<const>` tag tries to reassign to that variable
+- **Key finding**: The compiler treats `<const>` and `<let>` tags differently in terms of variable reassignment
+
+## Key Code Locations Found
+
+1. **`/testbed/packages/runtime-tags/src/translator/util/references.ts`**
+   - Handles `constantViolations` tracking
+   - Contains `trackAssignment` function
+   - Has `BindingType` enum with `let` type
+
+2. **`/testbed/packages/runtime-class/src/translator/tag/index.js`**
+   - Contains `constantViolations` handling
+   - Checks for assignment operations
+
+## Investigation Steps Completed
+
+1. ✅ Search for error message "Cannot assign to" - not found in packages
+2. ✅ Search for similar error patterns - found `constantViolations` handling  
+3. ✅ Identify key files dealing with assignment tracking
+4. ✅ Examine BindingType handling for `let` vs potential constant types
+
+## Next Steps
+
+1. Look for where the actual error message is generated (could be in Babel or TypeScript integration)
+2. Check how `<const>` and `<let>` tags are processed differently
+3. Find the code responsible for generating the specific error message
+4. Identify what changed between versions 6.0.55 and 6.0.56
+
+## Suspected Root Cause
+
+The error message style suggests it might be coming from:
+- TypeScript compiler integration
+- Babel transform that validates constant assignments
+- New strict mode validation added in version 6.0.56
+
+The error is specifically about trying to assign to a "constant" variable, which suggests the compiler is treating the `<const>`-declared variable as truly immutable, while `<let>` variables should be mutable.

+// Search for the error message in the codebase
+const fs = require('fs');
+const path = require('path');
+
+console.log('Searching for the error message "Cannot assign to"\n');
+
+const errorMessage = "Cannot assign to";
+const packagesDir = '/testbed/packages';
+
+function searchInDirectory(dir) {
+  const results = [];
+  
+  try {
+    const items = fs.readdirSync(dir);
+    for (const item of items) {
+      if (item === 'node_modules' || item === 'test' || item === 'dist') continue;
+      
+      const fullPath = path.join(dir, item);
+      try {
+        const stat = fs.statSync(fullPath);
+        
+        if (stat.isDirectory()) {
+          results.push(...searchInDirectory(fullPath));
+        } else if (stat.isFile() && (item.endsWith('.js') || item.endsWith('.ts'))) {
+          const content = fs.readFileSync(fullPath, 'utf8');
+          if (content.includes(errorMessage)) {
+            results.push(fullPath);
+            console.log(`Found in: ${fullPath}`);
+            
+            // Show context around the match
+            const lines = content.split('\n');
+            lines.forEach((line, i) => {
+              if (line.includes(errorMessage)) {
+                console.log(`  Line ${i+1}: ${line.trim()}`);
+                // Show surrounding lines for context
+                for (let j = Math.max(0, i-2); j <= Math.min(lines.length-1, i+2); j++) {
+                  if (j !== i) console.log(`    ${j+1}: ${lines[j].trim()}`);
+                }
+                console.log('');
+              }
+            });
+          }
+        }
+      } catch (e) {
+        // Skip files that can't be accessed
+      }
+    }
+  } catch (e) {
+    // Skip directories that can't be accessed
+  }
+  
+  return results;
+}
+
+console.log('Starting search...\n');
+const matches = searchInDirectory(packagesDir);
+
+if (matches.length === 0) {
+  console.log('Error message not found in packages directory');
+  console.log('\nLet me search for similar error patterns...\n');
+  
+  // Search for similar patterns
+  const patterns = [
+    'Cannot assign',
+    'constantViolations',
+    'constant violation',
+    'assignment to constant',
+    'you cannot reassign'
+  ];
+  
+  patterns.forEach(pattern => {
+    console.log(`Searching for "${pattern}"...`);
+    try {
+      const result = require('child_process').execSync(
+        `grep -r "${pattern}" /testbed/packages --include="*.js" --include="*.ts" --exclude-dir=node_modules -l | head -5`,
+        { encoding: 'utf8' }
+      );
+      if (result.trim()) {
+        console.log(`Found in files:\n${result}`);
+      }
+    } catch (e) {
+      // No matches found
+    }
+  });
+}

+      const fullPath = path.join(dir, item);
+      try {
+        const stat = fs.statSync(fullPath);
+        if (stat.isDirectory()) {
+          findTests(fullPath);
+        } else if (item.endsWith('.js') || item.endsWith('.marko')) {
+          if (!item.includes('node_modules') && !item.includes('fixtures')) {
+            files.push(fullPath);
+          }
+        }
+      } catch (e) {
+        // Skip files that can't be accessed
+      }
+    }
+  } catch (e) {
+    // Skip directories that can't be accessed
+  }
+}
+
+findTests(testDir);
+
+// Check if any test files have relevant content
+console.log(`Found ${files.length} test files`);
+

+// Simple test to use the compiler directly
+const { Module } = require('module');
+const fs = require('fs');
+
+// Patch require to handle ES modules gracefully
+const originalRequire = Module.prototype.require;
+Module.prototype.require = function(id) {
+  try {
+    return originalRequire.call(this, id);
+  } catch (error) {
+    if (error.code === 'ERR_UNSUPPORTED_DIR_IMPORT') {
+      // Try appending /index.js
+      return originalRequire.call(this, id + '/index.js');
+    }
+    throw error;
+  }
+};
+
+// Try to load the compiler
+console.log('Loading compiler...');
+try {
+  const compiler = require('./packages/compiler/dist/index.js');
+  console.log('Compiler loaded successfully!');
+  
+  // Now try to compile our test file
+  const markoCode = fs.readFileSync('./reproduce_issue.marko', 'utf8');
+  
+  console.log('Compiling marko code...');
+  const result = compiler.compile(markoCode, {
+    filename: 'reproduce_issue.marko',
+    output: 'source'
+  });
+  
+  console.log('COMPILATION SUCCESSFUL!');
+  console.log(result.code);
+} catch (error) {
+  console.error('ERROR:', error.message);
+  console.error(error.stack);
+}
